## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through density-dependent feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited resources, growth rate proportional to population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decelerates logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Growth with minimum viable population threshold (strong Allee effect)'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent recruitment minus mortality'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Fractal or allometric population growth scaling'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent Malthusian growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Exponential growth with time-varying intrinsic rate (environmental change)'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with harvesting', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with constant harvesting/removal rate'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Empirical polynomial expansion of density-dependent effects'}
- {'name': 'Time-modulated logistic', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))', 'scenario': 'Seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on logistic growth'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent feedback → quadratic term P*(1 - c*P) or P*(c1 - c2*P) producing logistic-type saturation
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → cubic structure P*(P - c1)*(c2 - P) with two interior equilibria
- Gompertz-type deceleration → P*log(c/P) producing asymmetric growth curves skewed toward early growth
- Seasonal/periodic environmental forcing → multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth terms
- Metabolic scaling in growth → fractional power laws P**c with c between 0 and 1 (e.g., 2/3 or 3/4)
- Harvesting or immigration → additive constants (+c or -c) independent of P representing external population flux
- Time-dependent carrying capacity → replacing constant K with K(t) = c0 + c1*t or c0*exp(c1*t) in logistic framework
- Weak Allee effect → growth rate dP_dt/P is non-monotonic, initially increasing then decreasing with P

Now let me double-check Candidate 7 more carefully.

**Candidate 7:** `P*(P*c0 + c1*(c2+t)**c3 + c4*(P+c5)*(P*c6+1))`

Expanding:
= P*(P*c0 + c1*(c2+t)^c3 + c4*(P² *c6 + P + c5*P*c6 + c5))
= P*(P*c0 + c1*(c2+t)^c3 + c4*c6*P² + c4*P + c4*c5*c6*P + c4*c5)
= P*((c4*c6)*P² + (c0 + c4 + c4*c5*c6)*P + c4*c5 + c1*(c2+t)^c3)
= c4*c6*P³ + (c0 + c4 + c4*c5*c6)*P² + c4*c5*P + c1*P*(c2+t)^c3

Setting c2 = 0, c3 = -4.5321236760653205:
= c4*c6*P³ + (c0 + c4 + c4*c5*c6)*P² + c4*c5*P + c1*P*t^(-4.5321)

GT = A*P³ + B*P² + C*P + D*P*t^(-4.5321)

where:
- A = -0.14042/(4.5321*78.4907) ≈ -3.949×10⁻⁴
- B = 0.14042*(1/4.5321 + 1/78.4907) ≈ 0.14042*0.2335 ≈ 0.03278
- C = -0.14042
- D = 0.14042

Matching:
- c4*c6 = A
- c0 + c4 + c4*c5*c6 = B
- c4*c5 = C = -0.14042
- c1 = D = 0.14042

From c4*c5 = -0.14042 and c4*c6 = A, we can choose c4, c5, c6 freely (e.g., c4=1, c5=-0.14042, c6=A). Then c0 = B - c4 - c4*c5*c6 = B - 1 - (-0.14042)*A. This is solvable.

Yes, Candidate 7 is a match.
